<response>None<//response>< text>
Opening Day - Definitely coming back. They opened on 2/3/17 so thought I'd go down and give it a try at lunch. They weren't quite ready at 11:30 so I went back at 2:30 pm. I ordered some food to share with the office. We got fish and chips with the New Zealand ocean perch, the Louisiana Catfish (and chips), and then 4 tempura jumbo shrimp.
The first thing that caught me was the price. The price is extremely reasonable.  All three items were less than $20 together. I waited about 8 minutes for the food to cook up. That seemed pretty speedy. When I got back to the office and opened the boxes, they contained the following:
1. 4 pieces of tempura jumbo shrimp. They were of good size and one of my coworkers was excited that they actually cleaned out the shrimp correctly.
2. 4 pieces of ocean perch and a couple handfuls of fries.
3. 4 pieces of catfish and a couple handfuls of fries.
4. 2 small containers of tartar sauce
5. 2 small containers of Frank's Red Hot sauce
6. A medium container of Cole Slaw
7. Napkins

It looked good, so we got some plates and took what we wanted. I love shrimp so that was the first thing I tried. It not only met my expectations, but exceeded them. Light batter, good quality shrimp. Then I tried the perch and chips. Again, light batter, juicy fish, good tasting overall. Fries were done just right, not soggy but not super crispy.  My co-worker who had the catfish said it reminded her of being in Mississippi.

We'll definitely be back. When replacing a historic business like The Mug, it's nice when the new place lives up to those expectations.<//text>

4<//Rating>
< review>
Every Goodwill location has it's strengths and weaknesses. This one's magor strength is it's book selection. This one I only recently discovered because it is so far across town, it's half way to Sebastopol...but I'm so glad I did find it! It is huge! I can't speak to the clothing or furniture much. It seems a bit dingy. I have found some decent kids clothes but it required a lot of digging. A decent knick knacks section, but again not in and of itself a draw. The books though, wow. When you walk in and look to your left it looks like a book store. I asked a staff 'why so many books?' and she told me that the lady who chooses what goes into this location really focusses on books, essentially curating what gets stocked. It's a beautiful thing. I love to bring my two girls here to come pick out a book as a treat. Great kids section! Another bonus is that this location stays open later than other Goodwills in town.</review>

<username>Kevin Mcnamee<//username><time>1621811325021<//time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
<Review>I hosted an 8.1 mile out and back hike on May 23, 2021 to Mount Baden-Powell. The parking is free directly at the trailhead and is free.

The trail is a moderate climb of 4 miles of switchbacks and with some pretty stunning views all the way up and down. I would say it's more of a moderate hike, I think if you have a few recent 10 mile or so hikes under your belt, you will do just fine. My favorite part is the last few hundred yards to the summit, where you have cliffs on both sides of you, I posted a video to my Google account.

Enjoy your hiking.< /Review>< pics>

<Rating>5</Rating><review>great historical place to visit. very peaceful trail. once you enter the main trail there is a fork with an unmarker sign. the right take you to the old mines, it is a bit of a hike but worth it, some parts can be a little difficult but take your time.
the left fork will take you to the old cabin, which still has some great artifacts which I am glad people are respecting and leaving untouched.
this trail is easy and relaxing to find the cabin can be a little confusing, on the trail you will hike a bit and come across a fallen tree or log on the right side of the trail. go over that log and continue on the trail for a little bit and the cabin comes into sight. there are plenty of youtube videos showing directions to the cabin. people are nice. We have been there several times with and without our dogs.

everyone for the most part has a mask on when they approach you .</review>< pictures>

< review>
The divide is home to a large paved parking area, a single bench under nearby trees, an information sign post (not frequently updated) and a restroom facility.  This area has no water (unless cached by Trail Angels) and no cell phone service (unless high up on the mountains). It is a starting point for several nearby trails. A Forest Adventure Pass is required to park here. Weekend activities are high and parking can fill up early.</review>

< review>
Perfect place to test the temperment of a future partner. The hike to Mt Baden-Powell is a real challenge, and is known for the many switchbacks. This is also the location where people drop in and hike to Bighorn Mine that goes down to Middle Earth. I've heard some gnarly stories about the mine and people passing out down there. Go with your gut instinct if you run out of air down there. The oak ladders will break as you try to get out. Follow the arrows.</review>

I absolutely love Bel Air and Raley's, I worked for Bel Air in 1990 and was a Meat clerk/Wrapper for the Meat Department.  I would go to whichever store needed coverage due to their meat clerk being out sick, on leave, vacation, etc.  I know Bel Air had very high standards in regards of customer service and products. <Text>Been a customer since the store first opened in 1991 or so. Had one of the original Bel Air Customer Cards. Had two children build careers through this store and then moving on/up in the Raley's System. My family has supported Bel Air / Raley's in numerous ways throughout the years. But recently was MOST disappointed in the new "check cashing" system.  Since last November, I've had checks denied four times. The first three times the store manager would come over and override the system and told me to call for him if it happens again. But the last time I was so angry I will do my best to put my money somewhere else.  The problem is not with my checks. I have never written a bad check. And the funds, in the last few years, are auto-deducted from my account just about immediately.

I called the number referred to on the "declined" receipt to find out why. And the reason? It's because Raley's management has arbitrarily put a dollar cap on the amount of checks they'll take from a customer within a certain amount of time. So basically, because I always write checks, I'm spending too much money?  Well alrighty then, I guess I'll take my "too much money" and spend it somewhere else.

Thanks, Raley's, for bringing this to my attention and embarrasing me for being such a loyal customer.<//Text>< Rate>
